Question: A company produces 420 units of a particular computer component every month, at a production cost to the company of $110 per component, and sells all of the components by the end of each month. What is the minimum selling price per component that will guarantee that the yearly profit (revenue from sales minus production costs) will be at least $626,400 ?
Choices:
  A: 226
  B: 230
  C: 240
  D: 260
  E: 280
Response 0:
Knowledge:
To find the minimum selling price per component, we need to determine the profit per component and then add it to the production cost per component. 
The profit per component will be the difference between the selling price and the production cost. 
We know that the company produces 420 units of the component every month, so the annual production will be 420 x 12 = 5040 units. 
We also know that the yearly profit should be at least $626,400.

Calculation:
Let's assume that the minimum selling price per component is x.
The revenue generated from selling one component will be x * 1 = x.
The profit generated from selling one component will be x - 110.
The profit generated from selling 5040 components will be (x - 110) * 5040.
We know that (x - 110) * 5040 >= 626400
Solving for x, we get x >= (626400/5040) + 110 = 230

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 50 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A starts travel towards south 3km, then travel 5 km towards east, and again travels 3 km to north, and finally travels 2km towards west. In the end how far from is A from home?
Choices:
  A: 3km
  B: 2km
  C: 4km
  D: 5km
  E: 6km
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  This is a problem involving finding the net displacement of the person who is traveling.
  We can use Pythagoras theorem to find the distance between two points in a 2D plane.
Action: 
  The person travels 3km towards south and then 3km towards north, so the net displacement in the north-south direction is 0.
  The person travels 5km towards east and then 2km towards west, so the net displacement in the east-west direction is 3km towards east.
  Therefore, the person is 3km away from home towards east.
  Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  This is a problem of finding the net displacement of A, which is the straight-line distance between the starting point and the final point of A's journey.

Question: What should come in place of the question mark(?) in each of the following questions ?
a2 - b2/(a + b)2 (?)=(a - b)2
Choices:
  A: (a + b)(a - b)
  B: (a - b)2
  C: (a + b)2
  D: a3 + b3
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Knowledge:
The identity (a-b)^2 = a^2 - 2ab + b^2 can be used to simplify the given expression.
We can also use the identity a^2 - b^2 = (a+b)(a-b) to simplify the numerator.

Solution:
a^2 - b^2 = (a+b)(a-b)
So, a^2 - b^2 / (a+b)^2 = (a+b)(a-b) / (a+b)^2
= (a-b)/(a+b)
Thus, the required value is (a-b)/(a+b)^2 = (a-b)^2 which is given in the question.
Therefore, the answer is (B) (a - b)2.

a2 - b2/(a + b)2 = a2 - 2ab + b2
=> b2/(a + b)2 = 2ab

b2 = 2ab(a + b)
=> b2 = 2a2b + 2ab2
=> b2 - 2a2b - 2ab2 = 0
=> -2(a2b + ab2 - b2) = 0
=> 2(b2 - a2b - ab2) = 0
=> 2b(b - a)(b + a) = 0

Therefore, b = 0 or a = -b.

Since the denominator cannot be zero, we have a + b ≠ 0.

Hence, we have a = -b.

Substituting a = -b in the given expression, we get:

a2 - b2/(a + b)2 = a2 - b2/0
=> Undefined

Therefore, the answer is E: None of these.

Question: A cyclist travels at 12 miles per hour. How many minutes will it take to travel 48 miles?
Choices:
  A: 1
  B: 240
  C: 30
  D: 60
  E: 120
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - 1 mile is equal to 1.60934 kilometers
  - The formula to calculate time is: time = distance / speed
  
Action: 
  - First, we need to convert the distance from miles to kilometers: 48 miles * 1.60934 km/mile = 77.24832 km
  - Then, we can use the formula to find the time: time = distance / speed = 77.24832 km / (12 miles/hour * 1.60934 km/mile) = 320.2432 / 12 hour = 26.687 hours
  - Finally, we need to convert the time from hours to minutes: 26.687 hours * 60 minutes/hour = 1601.22 minutes

Topic: Math
Question: Everyone in the family earns money each month. If the total income of a family per month is $9000 and the median income is $3000, how many members are there in the family?
Choices:
  A: 2
  B: 3
  C: 4
  D: 5
  E: 6
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - The median income is the middle value of a set of incomes when they are arranged in order.
  - If the median income is $3000, it means that half of the family members earn more than $3000 and half of them earn less than $3000.
  - If the total income of the family is $9000, it means that the average income per family member is $9000 divided by the number of family members.
Action: 
  - If the median income is $3000, it means that there are family members who earn less than $3000 and family members who earn more than $3000. 
  - If the total income of the family is $9000, and the median income is $3000, it means that there are three family members who earn $3000 each. 
  - Therefore, the answer is 3. 
  - Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Median is the middle value of a set of numbers.
  If the median income is $3000, then there are at least two people in the family.
  If the total income of a family is $9000, then the average income per person is $9000 divided by the number of family members.
  If the median income is $3000, then there are at least two people in the family earning $3000 each.
  Therefore, the remaining income ($9000 - 2*$3000) must be divided among the other family members.
  The number of family members will be the total income divided by the average income per person.
  So, the number of family members is $9000 / ($3000 + ($9000 - 2*$3000)/n), where n is the number of family members.

Action: Answer("C")

  Median is the middle value in a sorted list of numbers. If the list has an odd number of values, the median is the middle value. If the list has an even number of values, the median is the average of the two middle values.
  
Let's assume there are n members in the family. We know that the median income is $3000, which means that the income of the (n/2)th member is $3000. We also know that the total income of the family is $9000, which means that the average income per member is $9000/n.

If we combine these two pieces of information, we can set up an equation to solve for n:

(n/2) * $3000 + (n - n/2) * ($9000/n) = $9000

Simplifying this equation, we get:

(n/2) * $3000 + (n/2) * $9000/n = $9000

Multiplying both sides by 2/n, we get:

$3000 + $9000/n = $18000/n

Multiplying both sides by n, we get:

$3000n + $9000 = $18000

Subtracting $9000 from both sides, we get:

$3000n = $9000

Dividing both sides by $3000, we get:

n = 3

4. So, 2x/(8+10+2x) = 2/5

Let x be the number of months after B joined that C joined. So, C's investment was there for (12-x) months.
Total investment after C joined = 40000*12 + 60000*10 + 120000*(12-x) = 480000 + 120000x
Total profit ratio of A, B, and C = 2:3:x
Given that C's share of the profit was Rs.150,000
So, (x/(2+3+x)) * 375000 = 150000
Solving for x, we get x = 4
Therefore, C joined the business 4 months after B joined.
Action: Answer("B")

A's investment = Rs.40,000 for 12 months = Rs.480,000
B's investment = Rs.60,000 for 10 months (as he joined after 2 months) = Rs.600,000

Total investment = Rs.1,040,000

Total profit = Rs.375,000
C's share = Rs.150,000
Therefore, A and B's share = Rs.225,000 (375,000 - 150,000)

A's share ratio = 480,000/1,040,000 = 8/17
B's share ratio = 600,000/1,040,000 = 9/17
C's share ratio = 150,000/1,040,000 = 3/17

Let's assume that C joined after x months of B joining. Therefore, C was in business for (12-x) months.

Now, we can set up an equation using the ratios:
(9/17) * (12-x) + (3/17) * (12-x) = 5/17 * 12

Simplifying the equation:
12-x = 24/5
x = 60/5 - 12
x = 12

Therefore, C joined after 12 months, which is 4 months after B joined.

Topic: Math
Question: The sum of k consecutive integers is 51. If the least integer is -50, then k =
Choices:
  A: 40
  B: 62
  C: 82
  D: 92
  E: 102
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let n be the first integer in the sequence of k consecutive integers.
  The sum of k consecutive integers starting from n is k(n + (n + k - 1))/2 = k(2n + k - 1)/2.
  If the least integer is -50, then n = -50.
  We want to solve for k given that k(2n + k - 1)/2 = 51 and n = -50.

Calculation:
  Substituting n = -50 and simplifying the equation, we get:
  k(2(-50) + k - 1)/2 = 51
  k(-99 + k)/2 = 51
  -99k/2 + k^2/2 = 51
  k^2 - 99k - 102 = 0
  Using the quadratic formula, we get:
  k = (99 ± sqrt(99^2 + 4*1*102))/2
  k = (99 ± sqrt(9801 + 408))/2
  k = (99 ± sqrt(10209))/2
  k = (99 ± 101)/2
  Since k has to be a positive integer, we take the positive root:
  k = (99 + 101)/2 = 100/2 = 50

Answer: Answer("None of the Above") 

Explanation: 
  The answer is not one of the available choices. 
  The correct answer is k = 50, which is not listed among the choices.
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Let n be the first of k consecutive integers, then the sum of the k consecutive integers is k * n.
  The sum of the first n positive integers is n * (n+1) / 2.
  The sum of the first n negative integers is -n * (n-1) / 2.
  
Solution:
  If the least integer is -50, then the next integer is -49, and so on.
  Let's say we have k consecutive integers starting from -50, then the sum of these integers is:
  -50 + (-49) + (-48) + ... + (-50 + k - 1) = k * (-50) + (1 + 2 + 3 + ... + k - 1)
  We know that the sum of k consecutive integers is 51, so we have:
  k * (-50) + (1 + 2 + 3 + ... + k - 1) = 51
  k * (-50) + k * (k-1) / 2 = 51
  k * (-100 + k - 1) / 2 = 51
  k * (k - 101) = -102
  
  The only pair of factors of -102 that differ by an odd number is (-6, 17).
  Therefore, k = -6 or k = 17.
  
  We are looking for a positive value of k, so k = 17.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 59 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A certain liquid passes through a drain at a rate of w/25 gallons every x seconds. At that rate, how many minutes will it take y gallons to pass through the drain?
Choices:
  A: y/(1200xy)
  B: 20xy/w
  C: 5xy/(12w)
  D: w/(3xy)
  E: 3y/(wx)
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Rate = Amount of liquid passing through the drain / Time
  Amount of liquid passing through the drain = (w/25) gallons
  Time = x seconds
  We need to find the time in minutes, so we need to convert x seconds to minutes by dividing x by 60.
  We can then use the formula Time = Amount of liquid passing through the drain / Rate to find the time it takes for y gallons to pass through the drain.
  Therefore, Time = (y gallons) / [(w/25) gallons per x seconds] * [60 seconds per minute]

Calculations:
  Time = (y gallons) / [(w/25) gallons per x seconds] * [60 seconds per minute]
       = (y*25*60) / (w*x)
       = 150xy/w

Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - Rate = (amount of liquid passed) / (time taken).
  - The rate at which the liquid passes through the drain is w/25 gallons every x seconds.
  - To find the time taken for y gallons to pass through the drain, we need to find the rate at which the liquid passes through the drain in terms of y.
  - We can use the formula: time = amount / rate
  
Solution:
  - The rate at which the liquid passes through the drain is w/25 gallons every x seconds.
  - To find the rate at which the liquid passes through the drain in terms of y, we can use proportions:
      w/25 = y/time
      time = (25y)/w
  - We need to convert the time to minutes:
      time = (25y)/w * 1/60
      time = (5y)/(12w)
  - Therefore, the answer is (C) 5xy/(12w).

Topic: Math
Question: A square piece of cloth is trimmed by 4 feet on one edge to form a rectangular piece, which is then cut diagonally in half to create two triangles. If the area of each of triangle is 70 square feet, what was the perimeter (in feet) of the original piece of square cloth?
Choices:
  A: 56
  B: 58
  C: 60
  D: 62
  E: 64
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The area of a triangle is given by the formula (base x height)/2.
  The area of a square is given by the formula side^2.
  If a square piece of cloth is trimmed by 4 feet on one edge, the new rectangular piece will have dimensions (x-4) by x, where x is the original length of each side of the square.
  The diagonal of a rectangle can be found using the Pythagorean theorem: diagonal^2 = length^2 + width^2.
  The perimeter of a square is given by the formula 4 x side.
Action: 
  The area of each triangle is 70 square feet, so the product of the base and the height of each triangle is 140 square feet.
  Since the rectangular piece of cloth was formed by trimming 4 feet from one edge of the original square, its area is (x-4)x = x^2 - 4x square feet.
  The length of the rectangular piece can be found by dividing its area by the width: (x^2 - 4x)/x = x - 4 feet.
  The diagonal of the rectangular piece can be found using the Pythagorean theorem: diagonal^2 = (x-4)^2 + x^2.
  The diagonal of the rectangular piece is equal to the hypotenuse of one of the triangles, so we have diagonal^2 = 2(70) = 140.
  Substituting x-4 for diagonal in the equation above and solving for x, we get x = 14.
  Therefore, the perimeter of the original square piece of cloth is 4x = 56 feet.
  Answer: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - The area of a triangle can be calculated as (base * height) / 2.
  - The Pythagorean theorem states that, for a right triangle, the square of the length of the hypotenuse (the side opposite the right angle) is equal to the sum of the squares of the lengths of the other two sides.
  
Let x be the length of one edge of the original square piece of cloth.
After trimming 4 feet from one edge, the rectangular piece has dimensions (x-4) by x.
Cutting this rectangle in half diagonally creates two right triangles, each with base (x-4) and height x.
Thus, the area of each triangle is (base * height) / 2 = [(x-4) * x] / 2 = 70.
Solving for x, we get x = 14.
Therefore, the original piece of cloth had perimeter 4x = 4*14 = 56 feet.

    (x-4)^2 = 16

Question: A rectangular parking space is marked out by painting three of its sides. If the length of the unpainted side is 9 feet, and the sum of the lengths of the painted sides is 37 feet, then what is the area of the parking space in square feet?
Choices:
  A: 46
  B: 81
  C: 126
  D: 252
  E: None
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The painted sides form a rectangle with one side of length 9 feet.
  The sum of the lengths of the painted sides is 37 feet.
  Let the length of the rectangle be l and the width be w.
  The perimeter of the rectangle is 2l + w = 37.
  The unpainted side is w = 9.
  The area of the rectangle is A = lw.
Action: 
  Solving the system of equations, we get l = 14.5 and w = 9.
  The area of the rectangle is A = lw = 14.5 * 9 = 130.5 ≈ 126.
  Answer("C")

Question: Julie’s yard is rectangular. One side of the yard is 100 feet wide. The total area of the yard is 3,000 square feet. What is the length of the other side of the yard?
Choices:
  A: 30 feet
  B: 20 feet
  C: 10 feet
  D: 50 feet
  E: 60 feet
Response 0:

  - The formula for the area of a rectangle is A = l x w, where A is the area, l is the length, and w is the width.
  - We know that one side of the yard is 100 feet wide.
  - We know that the total area of the yard is 3,000 square feet.
  
Action: 
  - Let's call the length of the yard "l".
  - We can set up an equation using the formula for the area of a rectangle: A = l x w
  - We know that one side of the yard is 100 feet wide, so we can substitute that in for "w": A = l x 100
  - We also know that the total area of the yard is 3,000 square feet, so we can substitute that in for "A": 3,000 = l x 100
  - To solve for "l", we can divide both sides of the equation by 100: l = 30
  - Therefore, the length of the other side of the yard is 30 feet.

Question: Hoses A and B spout water at different constant rates, and hose A can fill a certain pool in 8 hours. Hose A filled the pool alone for the first 2 hours and the two hoses, working together, then finished filling the pool in another 3 hours. How many hours would it have taken hose B, working alone, to fill the entire pool?
Choices:
  A: 8
  B: 15
  C: 12
  D: 6
  E: 3
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Let's assume that Hose A fills the pool at a rate of x units per hour. 
  Then, Hose B fills the pool at a rate of y units per hour. 
  We can use the formula: rate = work done / time taken. 
  We can also use the formula: work done = rate x time taken.
  We know that hose A can fill the pool in 8 hours, so the work done by hose A in 1 hour is 1/8 of the pool. 
  We also know that the two hoses working together finished filling the pool in 3 hours, so the work done by both hoses in 1 hour is 1/3 of the pool. 
  We can use this information to form an equation and solve for y.

Working:
  In the first 2 hours, hose A filled 2/8 = 1/4 of the pool. 
  In the next 3 hours, both hoses working together filled 3/8 of the pool. 
  Therefore, the total work done is 1/4 + 3/8 = 5/8 of the pool. 
  We know that the rate of both hoses working together is 1/3 of the pool per hour. 
  So, we can set up the equation:
  x + y = 1/3     (both hoses working together)
  We also know that the rate of hose A alone is x = 1/8 of the pool per hour. 
  So, in the first 2 hours, hose A filled 2/8 = 1/4 of the pool. 
  Therefore, the remaining work that both hoses had to do together was 1 - 1/4 = 3/4 of the pool. 
  We can use the formula work done = rate x time taken to set up another equation:
  3/4 = (x + y) * 3
  We can now solve the system of equations:
  x + y = 1/3
  3x + 3y = 4/3
  Solving for x, we get x = 1/8. 
  Substituting x in the second equation, we get:
  3(1/8) + 3y = 4/3
  3y = 4/3 - 3/8
  3y = 17/24
  y = 17/72

Time taken by hose B to fill the pool = V / b = V / (1/16 V/hour) = 16 hours

Question: Two numbers are in the ratio 3:5. If 9 is subtracted from each, the new numbers are in the ratio 12:23. The smaller number is?
Choices:
  A: 21
  B: 33
  C: 35
  D: 42
  E: 58
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  If two numbers are in the ratio a:b, then they can be expressed as ax and bx, where x is a constant and a, b are the given ratio.
  If 9 is subtracted from each number, then the new numbers can be expressed as (ax - 9) and (bx - 9).
  If (ax - 9) and (bx - 9) are in the ratio c:d, then (ax - 9)/(bx - 9) = c/d.

Let the two numbers be 3x and 5x. 
Then, (3x - 9)/(5x - 9) = 12/23.
Solving for x, we get x = 69/8.
Therefore, the smaller number is 3x = 3*(69/8) = 207/8.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 65 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: If one of the roots of the quadratic equation x^2 + mx + 22 = 0 is 1.5, then what is the value of m?
Choices:
  A: -23.5
  B: -17.5
  C: -10.5
  D: -16.2
  E: Cannot be determined
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Quadratic equation in standard form: ax^2 + bx + c = 0
  The sum of the roots of a quadratic equation is -b/a.
  The product of the roots of a quadratic equation is c/a.
  
  We know one of the roots of the quadratic equation x^2 + mx + 22 = 0 is 1.5.
  Let's call the other root r.
  The sum of the roots is 1.5 + r = -m (from the quadratic equation in standard form).
  The product of the roots is 1.5 * r = 22 (from the quadratic equation in standard form).
  
  We can solve for r: r = 22/1.5 = 14.67.
  We can solve for m: 1.5 + 14.67 = -m, so m = -16.17 (rounded to the nearest hundredth).
Action: Answer("D")

Knowledge: 
  For a quadratic equation of the form ax^2 + bx + c = 0, the sum of the roots is -b/a and the product of the roots is c/a.

  The sum of the roots is (1.5 + 14.67) = 16.17.
  We can use the sum of the roots to find the value of m.
  A: -23.5 is not equal to 2m.
  B: -17.5 is not equal to 2m.
  C: -10.5 is not equal to 2m.
  D: -16.2 is equal to 2m, since (-16.2)/2 = -8.1 and (-8.1) + (1.5 + 14.67) = 16.17.

Topic: Math
Question: In a large forest, 300 deer were caught, tagged, and returned during 2001. During 2002, 500 deer were caught at random, of which only 20 had tags from the previous year. If the percent of deer in the forest that had tags during the second year and were caught in the 500 deer sample is representative of the percent of the total deer population in the forest with tags, what is the total deer population in the forest (assuming no change in population between 2001 and 2002)?
Choices:
  A: 300
  B: 500
  C: 5000
  D: 6000
  E: 7500
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Let P be the total deer population in the forest.
  During 2001, 300 deer were tagged and released, so the proportion of tagged deer in the forest is 300/P.
  During 2002, 500 deer were caught and 20 of them were tagged during 2001, so the proportion of tagged deer in the sample is 20/500 = 0.04.
  We are assuming that this proportion is representative of the proportion of tagged deer in the entire population, so we can set up the equation: 0.04 = 300/P.
Action: 
  Multiply both sides of the equation by P to get 0.04P = 300.
  Divide both sides by 0.04 to get P = 7500.
  Answer("E")

Question: On dividing 2272 and 875 by a 3-digit number N, we get the same remainder. The sum of the digits of N is:
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 11
  C: 12
  D: 13
  E: 14
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  If two numbers, a and b, leave the same remainder when divided by N, then their difference, a-b, is divisible by N.
  If a number is divisible by N, then the sum of its digits is also divisible by N.
  2272 and 875 are both positive integers.
Action: Answer("B") 

Let R be the common remainder when 2272 and 875 are divided by N.
Then we have: 
  2272 = k1N + R   ... (1)
   875 = k2N + R   ... (2)
where k1 and k2 are quotients.

Subtracting (2) from (1), we get:
  1397 = (k1-k2)N
Since 1397 is a prime number, it follows that k1-k2 = 1 and N = 1397.
Therefore, the sum of the digits of N is 1+3+9+7 = 20, which is divisible by N.
The sum of the digits of N is 2+0 = 2, which is not one of the choices.
However, 20 is also divisible by 10, so we can try to find a smaller number whose digits sum up to 10 and is divisible by 1397.
The only such number is 1099, whose digits sum up to 1+0+9+9 = 19, which is divisible by 1397.
Therefore, the answer is 1+0+9+9 = 19, which is equal to 10+9 = 19, and the closest choice is (B) 11.

Response 8:
Knowledge:
  If a number 'a' leaves the same remainder when divided by 'm' or 'n', then 'm' and 'n' must divide 'a-m' and 'a-n' respectively.
  The sum of the digits of a number is equal to the remainder when the number is divided by 9.
  If two numbers leave the same remainder when divided by a third number, then the difference between the two numbers must be divisible by the third number.
  
Solution:
Let the 3-digit number be N and the common remainder be R.
So, we can write:
  2272 = aN + R ...(i)
  875 = bN + R ...(ii)
where a and b are integers.

  1397 = (a-b)N

Therefore, the sum of the digits of N is 2 + 9 + 3 + 1 = 15.

  B: 8
  C: 22
  D: 50
  E: 20

  Jill's work rate is 5/100 times 1/12 of the yacht per hour, so she can do 1/3 of the yacht in (1/3) / ((5/100) times (1/12)) = 80 hours.

Question: Mr.Sam takes 17 hours to go by train to a certain city and return by car. He loses 4 hours if he goes both ways by train. How long would he have taken if he had traveled by car in both ways?
Choices:
  A: 22 hrs
  B: 18 hrs
  C: 16 hrs
  D: 20 hrs
  E: 13 hrs
Response 0:
Let's call the time it takes Mr. Sam to travel to the city by train "x". Then, we know that it takes him "17" hours to go by train to the city and return by car. Therefore, the time it takes him to return by car must be "(17 - x)" hours. We also know that if he goes both ways by train, he loses 4 hours, so it would take him "(2x + 4)" hours. Finally, we can set up the equation:

2x + 4 = 17 + (17 - x)

Simplifying this equation, we get:

3x = 30

x = 10

So, it takes Mr. Sam 10 hours to go to the city by train. Therefore, it takes him 7 hours to return by car. Thus, the total time it would take him to travel by car in both ways is:

7 + 7 = 14 hours

  The total value of all coins after one dive is $3.40 = 340 cents.
  
Calculation:
  We need to find the minimum number of copper coins that she brought.
  We can start by assuming that she brought only copper coins and no brass coins.
  If she brought 17 copper coins, the total value would be 20*17 = 340 cents, which matches the given total value.
  Therefore, the minimum number of copper coins that she brought is 17.
  Alternatively, we can use trial and error to find the solution.
  If she brought 16 copper coins, the total value of copper coins would be 20*16 = 320 cents.
  The remaining value of 340-320 = 20 cents can only come from one brass coin.
  However, the value of one brass coin is 25 cents, which is more than the remaining value of 20 cents.
  Therefore, she must have brought at least 17 copper coins.
  If she brought 18 copper coins, the total value of copper coins would be 20*18 = 360 cents.
  The excess value of 360-340 = 20 cents can only come from one copper coin.
  Therefore, she brought 17 copper coins and 1 brass coin.

Question: The sum of the digits of a three digit number is 17, and the sum of the squares of its digits is 109. If we subtract 495 from the number, we shall get a number consisting of the same digits written in the reverse order. Find the number.
Choices:
  A: 368
  B: 377
  C: 288
  D: 997
  E: 112
Response 0:
Let's call the hundreds digit x, the tens digit y, and the ones digit z. 

From the first condition, we know that:
x + y + z = 17 (Equation 1)

From the second condition, we know that:
x^2 + y^2 + z^2 = 109 (Equation 2)

Let's solve for one of the variables in terms of the others. From Equation 1, we know that:
x = 17 - y - z

We can substitute this into Equation 2:
(17 - y - z)^2 + y^2 + z^2 = 109

Simplifying and expanding:
289 - 34y - 34z + 2yz + 2zy + y^2 + z^2 = 109
y^2 + 2yz + z^2 - 34y - 34z + 180 = 0
(y + z)^2 - 34(y + z) + 180 = 0

We can solve for y + z using the quadratic formula:
y + z = (34 ± sqrt(34^2 - 4*1*180)) / 2
y + z = 17 ± 5

So either y + z = 22 or y + z = 12. 

We also know that the number is a three-digit number, so x cannot be 0. This means that y + z cannot be 12, since the maximum value of y or z is 9. Therefore, y + z must be 22.

Now we can use the third condition to find the number:
100x + 10y + z - 495 = 100z + 10y + x
99x - 99z = 495
x - z = 5

We know that x = 17 - y - z, so:
(17 - y - z) - z = 5
y + 2z = 12

We want to find a three-digit number where x + y + z = 17, y + z = 22, and x - z = 5. We can solve for x, y, and z:
x = 10
y = 12
z = 10

Therefore, the number is 100x + 10y + z = 1000 + 120 + 10 = 1130.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 73 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Fernando purchased a university meal plan that allows him to have a total of 3 lunches and 3 dinners per week. If the cafeteria is closed on weekends and Fernando always goes home for a dinner on Friday nights, how many options does he have to allocate his meals?
Choices:
  A: 5C3*4C3
  B: 5C4*4C2
  C: 5C2*4C4
  D: 5C6*4C5
  E: 4C3*4C3
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Fernando has 3 lunches and 3 dinners per week.
  Fernando goes home for dinner on Friday nights.
  The cafeteria is closed on weekends.
  Fernando has to allocate his meals for the remaining 5 days of the week.
  The number of ways to choose k items from n distinct items is given by the combination formula C(n,k) = n! / (k! * (n-k)!).
  
Analysis: 
  Fernando has 2 options for Friday dinner (either eat at home or on campus).
  Fernando has 5 options for each of the remaining 5 days of the week (either lunch or dinner).
  Fernando has to choose 2 out of 5 options for the remaining 5 days for lunch.
  Fernando has to choose 3 out of 5 options for the remaining 5 days for dinner.
  The total number of options is the product of the number of options for each decision.

Action: Answer("A")  
Explanation: 
  Fernando has 2 options for Friday dinner.
  Fernando has 5 options for each of the remaining 5 days of the week (either lunch or dinner).
  Fernando has to choose 2 out of 5 options for the remaining 5 days for lunch, which is 5C2.
  Fernando has to choose 3 out of 5 options for the remaining 5 days for dinner, which is 5C3.
  The total number of options is 2 * 5C2 * 5C3 = 10 * 10 = 100.

Question: The ratio of the volumes of a cube to that of the sphere which will fit inside the cube is?
Choices:
  A: 2: π
  B: 7:2
  C: 8:2
  D: 6: π
  E: 8:3
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The volume of a cube with side length 'a' is given by a^3.
  The volume of a sphere with radius 'r' is given by (4/3)πr^3.
  The diameter of the sphere which will fit inside the cube is equal to the side length of the cube.
  The ratio of the volumes of the cube to that of the sphere which will fit inside the cube is given by (a^3) / [(4/3)π(a/2)^3] = (a^3) / [(4/3)π(a^3/8)] = 6/π.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The volume of a cube is given by V_cube = s^3, where s is the length of its side.
  The volume of a sphere is given by V_sphere = (4/3)πr^3, where r is the radius of the sphere.
  If a sphere is inscribed inside a cube, then its diameter is equal to the side length of the cube.
  The ratio of the volumes of a cube to that of the sphere which will fit inside the cube is V_cube / V_sphere.

To solve the problem, we need to find the relationship between the side length of the cube and the radius of the sphere. Let s be the side length of the cube, then the diameter of the sphere is equal to s. Hence, the radius of the sphere is r = s/2.

Now, we can write the ratio of the volumes as follows:
V_cube / V_sphere = s^3 / [(4/3)π(s/2)^3]
                  = 3s^3 / 4πs^3
                  = 3 / (4π)

  C: 126
  D: 252
  E: 525

  The formula for the number of ways to divide n objects into k groups is given by n choose k, which is denoted as C(n,k) or  .
  The formula for n choose k is n! / (k! * (n-k)!), where n! denotes the factorial of n, which is the product of all positive integers up to n.

Topic: Math
Question: All 250 files on Sam's hard drive are infected by either a virus or a worm or both. The number of files that are infected only by a worm is 2.5 times the number of files that are infected by both a virus and a worm. If 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, how many of Sam's files were NOT infected by a worm?
Choices:
  A: 50
  B: 70
  C: 75
  D: 100
  E: 125
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - Let V be the number of files infected by a virus.
  - Let W be the number of files infected by a worm.
  - Let VW be the number of files infected by both a virus and a worm.
  - We know that V + W - VW = 250 (since all files are either infected by a virus, a worm, or both).
  - We also know that W - VW = 2.5 * VW (since the number of files that are infected only by a worm is 2.5 times the number of files that are infected by both a virus and a worm).
  - We know that 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, so V = 0.5 * 250 = 125.
Action: 
  Using the above knowledge, we can solve for the number of files infected by a worm:
  V + W - VW = 250
  125 + W - VW = 250 (since V = 125)
  W - VW = 125
  1.5 * VW = 125 (since W - VW = 2.5 * VW, we can substitute W - VW with 2.5 * VW to get 1.5 * VW)
  VW = 83.33
  W - 83.33 = 2.5 * 83.33
  W = 249.99
  Therefore, the number of files NOT infected by a worm is:
  250 - W = 0.01

  250 = 125 + (125 - 2.5x) + x

  We also know that 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, so V = 0.5(250) - B.
Action: 
  We can use the equations above to solve for the value of B. 
  Substituting W = 2.5B into V + W + B = 250, we get V + 3.5B = 250. 
  Substituting V = 0.5(250) - B into the equation above, we get 0.5(250) - B + 3.5B = 250. 
  Simplifying the equation, we get B = 40. 
  Therefore, the number of files infected only by a worm is W = 2.5B = 100. 
  The number of files not infected by a worm is 250 - W = 150. 
  Since 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, the number of files infected by a virus is V = 0.5(250) - B = 85. 
  Therefore, the number of files not infected by a worm is 150 - (250 - V - W) = 150 - (250 - 85 - 100) = 85. 
  Answer: Answer("D")

  W = 2.5X

  Therefore, we have: 250 = (V + X) + (W + X) - X + Neither
  Simplifying this equation, we get: Neither = 250 - V - 1.5X

  B: 300
  C: 280
  D: 320
  E: 315

  Profit = Selling Price - Cost Price
  A: Calculation mistake
  B: Calculation mistake
  C: Calculation mistake
  D: Calculation mistake
  E: Calculation mistake

  Selling Price = Rs. 360

  Selling Price = Cost Price + Profit
  Rs. 360 = Cost Price + (20/100)*Cost Price
  Rs. 360 = Cost Price * (1 + 20/100)
  Cost Price = Rs. 360 / (1 + 20/100)
  Cost Price = Rs. 300
  Answer: Answer("B")

  Profit % = (Profit / Cost Price) * 100

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 78 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A newspaper costs $4 on Sunday and $1 the rest of the days of the week. If a hotel orders twice as many papers on Sunday as it does the rest of the days of the week and pays $210 per week for newspapers, how many newspapers does it buy on Monday?
Choices:
  A: 15
  B: 30
  C: 45
  D: 60
  E: 75
Response 0:
Knowledge:
Let's assign variables to the unknowns:
- Let x be the number of newspapers bought on a day that is not Sunday.
- Let y be the number of newspapers bought on Sunday.
- The cost of a newspaper on Sunday is $4, while the cost of a newspaper on any other day is $1.
- The hotel pays $210 per week for newspapers.

We can set up the following equations:
1. y = 2x (the hotel orders twice as many papers on Sunday as it does the rest of the days of the week)
2. 4y + x(7 - 1) = 210 (the total cost of the newspapers for the week is $210)

Action: 
1. Substitute y = 2x from equation 1 into equation 2:
   4(2x) + x(7 - 1) = 210
   8x + 6x = 210
   14x = 210
   x = 15
2. The hotel buys x newspapers on Monday, which is the day after Sunday. Therefore, the answer is A: 15. Answer("A")
Response 1:
Let's start by defining some variables to help us solve the problem:
- x: number of newspapers the hotel orders on Monday
- 2x: number of newspapers the hotel orders on Sunday
- 6x: total number of newspapers the hotel orders from Monday to Saturday
- 2(4) = 8: cost of the newspapers the hotel orders on Sunday
- 6(1) = 6: cost of the newspapers the hotel orders from Monday to Saturday
- 8 + 6 = 14: total cost of the newspapers per week
- 210/14 = 15: number of weeks the hotel orders newspapers
Now we can solve for x:
- 2x + x = 3x: total number of newspapers the hotel orders per week
- 8 + 6x = 210/15 = 14: total cost of the newspapers per week
- 6x = 14 - 8 = 6: cost of the newspapers from Monday to Saturday
- x = 6/6 = 1: number of newspapers the hotel orders on Monday
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume that the hotel buys x newspapers on Monday. 
  The hotel buys 2x newspapers on Sunday.
  The hotel buys x newspapers for the rest of the days of the week.
  The cost of a newspaper on Sunday is $4.
  The cost of a newspaper on the rest of the days of the week is $1.
  The hotel pays $210 per week for newspapers.
  
Calculation:
  The cost of the newspapers on Sunday is 4(2x) = 8x dollars.
  The cost of the newspapers on the rest of the days of the week is 1(x) = x dollars.
  The total cost of the newspapers is 8x + x + 4(x) = 13x + 4 dollars.
  We know that the total cost of the newspapers is $210.
  So, we can set up the equation 13x + 4 = 210 and solve for x.
  13x = 206
  x = 15.85 (rounded to two decimal places)
  Since the hotel can't buy a fraction of a newspaper, it must buy 15 newspapers on Monday.
  
Action: Answer("A")

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 80 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Allen starts from X, goes to Y. At the same time Bob starts from Y and goes towards X. Once Allen reaches Y he changes his direction and returns to X. Once Bob reaches X, he changes his direction and returns to Y. Throughout Allen travels at 54 kmph and Bob travels at 78kmph. By the time they meet for the second time, Bob covers 48 km more than Allen. Find the distance between X and Y.
Choices:
  A: 144km
  B: 72 km
  C: 126km
  D: 84 km
  E: 48km
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  - The distance traveled by Allen and Bob from X to Y is the same as the distance traveled by Bob and Allen from Y to X.
  - Let's assume the distance between X and Y is d.
  - Let's assume the time they meet for the first time is t.
  - The distance traveled by Allen from X to Y is d. Therefore, the distance traveled by Bob from Y to X is also d.
  - The distance traveled by Allen from Y to X is (d - 48). Therefore, the distance traveled by Bob from X to Y is also (d - 48).
  - We can use the formula distance = speed x time to form two equations:
    - d = 54t + 78t
    - d - 48 = 54t + 78t
  - We can simplify these equations to:
    - d = 132t
    - d = 132t + 48
  - We can solve for d by equating the right-hand side of these equations:
    - 132t = 132t + 48
    - 48 = 0t + 48
    - t = 1
    - d = 132t = 132 km
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - Distance, speed, and time are related by the formula: distance = speed x time
  - When two objects move towards each other, the relative speed is the sum of their individual speeds.
  - When two objects move in opposite directions, the relative speed is the difference between their individual speeds.
  - The time taken by two objects to meet each other is given by the formula: time = distance / relative speed
  
Let the distance between X and Y be d.
Let the time taken by Allen to reach Y be t.
Then, the time taken by Bob to reach X is also t.
When they meet for the first time, the total distance covered by both of them is d.
Relative speed of Allen and Bob when they move towards each other = 54 + 78 = 132 kmph
Time taken to meet for the first time = d / 132
Distance covered by Allen = 54t
Distance covered by Bob = 78t
Since they meet for the second time, the distance covered by Allen and Bob is 2d.
Relative speed of Allen and Bob when they move towards each other = 54 + 78 = 132 kmph
Relative speed of Allen and Bob when they move away from each other = 78 - 54 = 24 kmph
Let the time taken by Allen to reach X be t1.
Then, the time taken by Bob to reach Y is also t1.
Total time taken by Allen and Bob to meet for the second time = t + t1
Distance covered by Allen = 54(t + t1)
Distance covered by Bob = 78(t + t1) + 48 (since Bob covers 48 km more than Allen)
Distance covered by Allen and Bob = 2d
54(t + t1) + 78(t + t1) + 48 = 2d
132(t + t1) = 2d - 48
t + t1 = (d - 24) / 66
Substituting this value in the equation for distance covered by Allen and Bob, we get:
54(t + t1) + 78(t + t1) + 48 = 2d
132(t + t1) = 2d - 48
132[(d - 24) / 66] = 2d - 48
4(d - 24) = 2d - 48
2d = 96
d = 48 km

  - Distance = Speed x Time

When Allen and Bob meet for the first time, their combined distance covered is d, and their relative speed is 54 + 78 = 132 kmph.
Therefore, using the formula Distance = Speed x Time, we can say that:
d = 132t

After they meet for the first time, Allen still has to cover the distance from Y to X, which is also d. Bob still has to cover the distance from X to Y, which is also d.
Therefore, the total distance covered by Bob in this round trip is 2d + 48 km (48 km more than Allen).
The time it takes for Allen to cover the distance from Y to X is the same as the time it takes for Bob to cover the distance from X to Y, since they are both traveling at the same speed.
Let's call this time "t2".
Using the formula Distance = Speed x Time, we can say that:
d = 54t2
2d + 48 = 78t2

Now we have two equations with two unknowns (d and t2):
d = 54t2
2d + 48 = 78t2

We can solve for t2 by substituting the first equation into the second equation:
2(54t2) + 48 = 78t2
108t2 + 48 = 78t2
30t2 = 48
t2 = 48/30 = 8/5 hours

Now we can substitute t2 back into the first equation to find d:
d = 54t2
d = 54 x 8/5
d = 86.4 km

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 82 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The number of water lilies on a certain lake doubles every two days. If there is exactly one water lily on the lake, it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies. In how many days will the lake be fully covered with lilies, if initially there were 64 water lilies on it?
Choices:
  A: 15
  B: 28
  C: 30
  D: 53
  E: 59
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The number of water lilies doubles every two days.
  If there is one lily initially, it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered.
  If there are 64 lilies initially, we need to find out how many days it will take for the lake to be fully covered.

Solution:
  Let's start by finding out the number of days it takes for the lilies to double from 1 to 64.
  2^6 = 64, so it takes 6 * 2 = 12 days for the lilies to double 6 times and reach 64.
  Now, we know that it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered starting from 1 lily.
  So, it takes 60 - 12 = 48 days for the lake to be fully covered starting from 64 lilies.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  If the number of water lilies doubles every two days, then the growth is exponential and can be modeled by the equation y = a * 2^(t/k), where y is the number of water lilies, t is the time in days, a is the initial number of water lilies, and k is the doubling time in days.
  
  If there is exactly one water lily on the lake, it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies, then we can use the equation y = a * 2^(t/k) and the information given to solve for k:
  2^(60/k) = 2^6
  60/k = 6
  k = 10
  
  If initially there were 64 water lilies on the lake, then a = 64.
  
  We want to find the time it takes for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies, which means y = 2^6 * 64 = 4096.
  
  We can use the equation y = a * 2^(t/k) and the values we have to solve for t:
  4096 = 64 * 2^(t/10)
  2^(t/10) = 64
  t/10 = 6
  t = 60

    - 6 = (t/2) * 1
    - t = 12

Topic: Math
Question: The average (arithmetic mean) of the weight of 10 vehicles is 12.2 tons. The average weight of the group of vehicles increased by 2.6 tons after a new heavy duty truck was added to the group? What is the weight in tons of the heavy duty truck?
Choices:
  A: 40.8
  B: 41.6
  C: 42.2
  D: 43.5
  E: 44.8
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The formula for the arithmetic mean is: sum of the items / number of items.
  Let x be the weight of the heavy duty truck.
  The sum of the weights of the 10 original vehicles is 10 * 12.2 = 122.
  After the new truck is added, the sum of the weights of all 11 vehicles is (10 * 12.2) + x.
  The new average is (10 * 12.2 + x) / 11.
  We can set up an equation: (10 * 12.2 + x) / 11 = 12.2 + 2.6.
Action: Answer("B")  
Solution:
  Simplify the equation: (122 + x) / 11 = 14.8.
  Multiply both sides by 11: 122 + x = 162.8.
  Subtract 122 from both sides: x = 40.8.
  Therefore, the weight of the heavy duty truck is 40.8 tons.
  The answer is A.
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The formula to calculate the arithmetic mean is: sum of all values / number of values.
  If the average of a group of values is increased by adding a new value, then the sum of all values in the group is increased by the difference between the new average and the old average.
  
Solution:
  Let x be the weight of the heavy duty truck in tons.
  The sum of the weights of the 10 initial vehicles is 10 * 12.2 = 122 tons.
  After adding the new truck, the sum of the weights of all 11 vehicles is (10*12.2) + x = 122 + x tons.
  The new average weight of the group is (122 + x) / 11 tons.
  We know that the new average is 2.6 tons greater than the old average, so:
  (122 + x) / 11 - 12.2 = 2.6
  (122 + x) / 11 = 14.8
  122 + x = 162.8
  x = 40.8

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 85 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: 10kg of a mixture contains 30% sand and 70% clay. In order to make the mixture contain equal quantities of clay and sand how much of the mixture is to be removed and replaced with pure sand?
Choices:
  A: 10/7
  B: 20/7
  C: 30/7
  D: 40/7
  E: 50/7
Response 0:
Let's start by finding the amount of sand and clay in the original mixture. 

Amount of sand = 30% of 10kg = 3kg
Amount of clay = 70% of 10kg = 7kg

Let's assume we remove and replace x kg of the mixture with pure sand. After this operation, the amount of sand will be (3-x) kg and the amount of clay will still be 7 kg. The total weight of the mixture will still be 10 kg. 

We want the mixture to contain equal quantities of sand and clay. This means that the amount of sand should be equal to the amount of clay. 

3-x = 7
x = 4

So we need to remove and replace 4kg of the mixture with pure sand. 

Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Total mixture = 10kg
  Sand = 30% of 10kg = 3kg
  Clay = 70% of 10kg = 7kg

  Sand = 3kg
  Clay = 7kg - (7kg/10kg)*x = 7 - (7/10)*x
  Total mixture = 10kg - x
  
We want the mixture to contain equal quantities of sand and clay. Therefore, we can write the following equation:
  3 = (1/2)(7 - (7/10)*x)
  
Solving for x, we get:
  x = 20/7

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 88 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: What will be the cost of gardening 1-metre – broad boundary around a rectangular plot having perimeter of 340 metres at the rate of 10 per square metre?
Choices:
  A: 3400
  B: 1700
  C: 3440
  D: Cannot be determined
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Perimeter of a rectangle = 2(length + breadth)
  Let's assume the length of the rectangular plot is L and the breadth is B. 
  The perimeter of the plot, P = 2(L + B) = 340m
  Cost of gardening per square meter = 10
  We need to find the cost of gardening 1-meter broad boundary around the rectangular plot, which means we need to find the area of the rectangular plot after reducing 1 meter from both sides of the length and breadth.
  The area of the rectangular plot = (L - 2)(B - 2)
  The area of the 1-meter broad boundary = 2(L+B-4)
  Total cost of gardening = Area x Cost per square meter

Calculation:
  2(L+B-4) = P
  L+B = P/2 + 4
  L+B = 340/2 + 4 = 174
  (L-2)(B-2) = LB - 2L - 2B + 4
  (L-2)(B-2) = LB - (L+B) + 4
  (L-2)(B-2) = LB - 174 + 4
  (L-2)(B-2) = LB - 170
  Total cost of gardening = (L-2)(B-2) x Cost per square meter = (LB - 170) x 10

Action: Answer("C") 
Therefore, the total cost of gardening will be (LB - 170) x 10 = (174*2 - 170) x 10 = 3440.
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  Perimeter of a rectangle = 2(Length + Breadth)
  The perimeter of the rectangular plot is given as 340 metres.
  Let the length and breadth of the rectangular plot be L and B, respectively.
  The cost of gardening 1-metre broad boundary around the rectangular plot will be equal to the cost of gardening the outer rectangle with length (L+2) and breadth (B+2) minus the cost of gardening the inner rectangle with length (L) and breadth (B).
  The cost of gardening 1 square metre is given as 10.
Action: 
  Perimeter of the rectangular plot = 2(L + B) = 340
  L + B = 170
  Let the cost of gardening the outer rectangle be C1, and the cost of gardening the inner rectangle be C2.
  C1 = 10 * (L+2) * (B+2)
  C2 = 10 * L * B
  Cost of gardening 1-metre broad boundary = C1 - C2
  = 10 * (L+2) * (B+2) - 10 * L * B
  = 10 * (LB + 2L + 2B + 4)
  = 10 * (LB + 2(L+B) + 4)
  = 10 * (LB + 2*170 + 4)
  = 10 * (LB + 344)
  We cannot determine the value of LB from the given information, but we can calculate the cost of gardening the 1-metre broad boundary using the above formula.
Answer: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  Perimeter of a rectangle = 2(length + breadth).
  Let the length and breadth of the rectangular plot be L and B, respectively.
  Then, 2(L+B) = 340, which implies L+B = 170.
  The cost of gardening 1 square metre is 10.
  The cost of gardening the 1-meter broad boundary around the rectangular plot will be the same as the cost of gardening the rectangular plot with length and breadth increased by 2 meters each.
  The area of the rectangular plot with length and breadth increased by 2 meters each is (L+2)(B+2).
  The area of the rectangular plot is L*B.
  The area of the 1-meter broad boundary around the rectangular plot is (L+2)(B+2) - L*B.
Action: 
  The length and breadth of the rectangular plot can be determined as follows:
  L+B = 170  => B = 170 - L
  2(L+B) = 340 => L + B = 170
  L + (170 - L) = 170 => L = 85
  B = 170 - L = 85
  The area of the rectangular plot is L*B = 85*85 = 7225 square meters.
  The area of the rectangular plot with length and breadth increased by 2 meters each is (L+2)(B+2) = (85+2)(85+2) = 7396 square meters.
  The area of the 1-meter broad boundary around the rectangular plot is (L+2)(B+2) - L*B = 7396 - 7225 = 171 square meters.
  The cost of gardening the 1-meter broad boundary around the rectangular plot at the rate of 10 per square meter is 171*10 = 1710.
  Answer("B")
Response 3:
Knowledge:
  Perimeter of a rectangle = 2(Length + Breadth)
  Let L be the length and B be the breadth of the rectangular plot.
  Then, 2(L + B) = 340, which simplifies to L + B = 170.
  Area of the rectangular plot = Length x Breadth = L x B
  Area of the plot with a 1-metre boundary = (L+2) x (B+2)
  Cost of gardening per square metre = 10
Calculation:
  L + B = 170, which means (L+2) + (B+2) = 174
  Area of the plot with a 1-metre boundary = (L+2) x (B+2) = (L x B) + 2(L + B) + 4
  Area of the plot with a 1-metre boundary = (L x B) + 2(L + B) + 4 = (L x B) + 2(170) + 4 = (L x B) + 344
  Cost of gardening the 1-metre boundary = Cost per square metre x Area of the plot with a 1-metre boundary
  Cost of gardening the 1-metre boundary = 10 x [(L x B) + 344]
Action: Answer("C")
Response 4:
Knowledge:
  The perimeter of a rectangle is the sum of the lengths of all its sides.
  The perimeter of a rectangle with length L and width W is given by P = 2L + 2W.
  The cost of gardening a rectangular plot with length L and width W and a 1-meter broad boundary is given by C = (P + 4) * 10, where P is the perimeter of the rectangle.
  
Calculation:
  Let L and W be the length and width of the rectangular plot, respectively.
  We know that P = 2L + 2W = 340.
  Solving for L, we get L = 170 - W.
  The area of the rectangular plot with length L and width W is given by A = LW.
  The area of the rectangular plot with a 1-meter broad boundary is given by (L+2)*(W+2).
  The area of the 1-meter broad boundary is (L+2)*(W+2) - LW.
  So, the total area to be gardened is A' = (L+2)*(W+2) - LW.
  Substituting L = 170 - W, we get A' = 344 - W.
  The cost of gardening the area A' is C = A' * 10.
  Substituting A' = 344 - W, we get C = (344 - W) * 10 = 3440 - 10W.

Action: Answer("C")

  New perimeter = 2(L+2 + W+2) = 2(L+W+4) = 2(170+4) = 348
  Area of the rectangular plot = L x W
  Area of the plot with boundary = (L+2) x (W+2)
  Area of the boundary = (L+2) x (W+2) - L x W
  Cost of gardening = Area of the boundary x Rate per square metre

                       = LW + 2L + 2W + 4 - LW
                       = 2L + 2W + 4
                       = 2(L+W+2)
                       = 2(170+2)
                       = 344

                    = 344 x 10

Question: Calculate the percentage gain of a merchant who purchased 90 kg of oranges for Rs. 450 and sold the whole lot at the rate of Rs. 7.50 per kg.
Choices:
  A: 50 %
  B: 60 %
  C: 55 %
  D: 70 %
  E: 58%
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Percentage gain is calculated as (Profit/Cost Price) * 100
  Cost Price is the price at which the merchant purchased the oranges.
  Profit is the difference between the selling price and the cost price.
  Selling price is the price at which the merchant sold the oranges.
  The merchant purchased 90 kg of oranges for Rs. 450, so the cost price of each kg of oranges is 450/90 = Rs. 5.
  The merchant sold the whole lot at the rate of Rs. 7.50 per kg. So, the selling price of 90 kg of oranges is 90 * 7.50 = Rs. 675.
  Profit = Selling Price - Cost Price = 675 - 450 = Rs. 225.
Action: Answer("B")  
Profit Percentage = (Profit/Cost Price) * 100
Profit Percentage = (225/450) * 100 = 50% * (3/2) = 60%. 
So, the percentage gain of the merchant is 60%.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 93 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Joe's age, Joe's sister's age and Joe’s fathers age sums up to 100. When Joe is as old as his father, Joe's sister will be twice as old as now. When Joe is as old as his father then his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father. Find the age of Joe's father?
Choices:
  A: 45
  B: 48
  C: 50
  D: 55
  E: 58
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let's represent Joe's age, Joe's sister's age, and Joe's father's age by j, s, and f respectively.
  From the first statement, we know that j + s + f = 100.
  In the second statement, we know that when Joe is as old as his father, we have j + f = 2(s+1).
  In the third statement, we know that when Joe is as old as his father, we have f = 2(s - (j-f)).
  We can use these equations to solve for f.

Solution:
  From the first statement, we have j + s + f = 100.
  From the second statement, we have j + f = 2(s+1).
  Rearranging the second equation, we get s = (j+f-2)/2.
  Substituting s into the third equation, we get f = 2((j+f-2)/2 - (j-f)).
  Simplifying the equation, we get f = 3j/2 - 3f + 2.
  Rearranging the equation, we get 5f/2 = 3j + 2.
  Substituting j + s + f = 100 and s = (j+f-2)/2 into the equation, we get 5f/2 = 3j + j + f - 98.
  Simplifying the equation, we get 3j = f + 98.
  Substituting 3j = f + 98 into j + s + f = 100, we get j + s = 1.

2S - J = F     (Equation 4)

3S = 100

66.67 - J = 66.66 - 2J
J = 0.01

2S - J = F
2(33.33) - 0.01 = F
66.66 = F

  Simplifying this equation, we get J = 40.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 94 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Christopher and Jonathan were having bets. They decide that a coin will be flipped twenty times and each time it turns heads, Christopher will give $2 to Jonathan and each time it turns out to be Tails, Jonathan will give 3$ to Christopher. After flipping for twenty times none of the both won or lost any amount.
How many times did the coin landed on Heads ?
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 23
  C: 16
  D: 18
  E: 12
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  For every head, Christopher gives $2 to Jonathan.
  For every tail, Jonathan gives $3 to Christopher.
  After flipping the coin 20 times, neither of them won or lost any money.
  We need to find out the number of times the coin landed on heads.
  Let's say the coin landed on heads n times.
  Then, Christopher gave a total of 2n dollars to Jonathan.
  Jonathan gave a total of 3(20-n) dollars to Christopher.
  Since neither of them won or lost any money, we can set their total payments equal to each other.
  That gives us the equation 2n = 60 - 3n.
  Solving for n, we get n = 12.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  Each time the coin lands on Heads, Christopher will give $2 to Jonathan.
  Each time the coin lands on Tails, Jonathan will give $3 to Christopher.
  After flipping the coin twenty times, neither Christopher nor Jonathan won or lost any amount.
  Let's assume that the coin landed on Heads x times.
Action: 
  Each time the coin landed on Heads, Christopher gave $2 to Jonathan. Therefore, Christopher gave a total of 2x dollars to Jonathan.
  Each time the coin landed on Tails, Jonathan gave $3 to Christopher. Therefore, Jonathan gave a total of 3(20 - x) = 60 - 3x dollars to Christopher.
  Since neither Christopher nor Jonathan won or lost any amount, we can set up the following equation: 
  2x = 60 - 3x
  Solving for x, we get:
  5x = 60
  x = 12
  Therefore, the coin landed on Heads 12 times.

Topic: Math
Question: Kevin drove from A to B at a constant speed of 70 mph. Once he reached B, he turned right around with pause, and returned to A at a constant speed of 90 mph. Exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it. What is the distance between A and B?
Choices:
  A: 180
  B: 90
  C: 270
  D: 360
  E: None of the above
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  - The formula to calculate distance is distance = rate x time.
  - Let's call the distance between A and B as "d". 
  - Let's call the time it takes Kevin to drive from A to B as "t1".
  - Let's call the time it takes Kevin to drive from B to A as "t2".
  - We know that Kevin drives at 70 mph from A to B and at 90 mph from B to A.
  - We also know that 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it. This means that he had already driven (d - 70) miles by that time.
Action: 
  - Let's first calculate the time it takes Kevin to drive from A to B:
    - distance = rate x time
    - d = 70t1
    - t1 = d/70
  - Now let's calculate the time it takes Kevin to drive from B to A:
    - distance = rate x time
    - d = 90t2
    - t2 = d/90
  - We know that 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it. This means that he had already driven (d - 70) miles by that time.
  - We also know that there were 3 hours left in his trip at that point. This means that the total time for his trip is (t1 + t2 - 3).
  - We can now write an equation for the total distance he drove:
    - d = 70t1 + 90t2
    - d = 70(d/70) + 90(d/90)
    - d = d + d
    - d = 2d
  - We can now write an equation for the time it took him to drive from A to (d - 70) miles away from B:
    - (d - 70) = 70t1
    - t1 = (d - 70)/70
  - We can also write an equation for the time it took him to drive from (d - 70) miles away from B to A:
    - 70 = 90t2
    - t2 = 70/90
  - We can now write an equation for the total time for his trip:
    - (t1 + t2 - 3) = (d - 70)/70 + 70/90 - 3
    - (t1 + t2 - 3) = (d - 70)/70 + 7/9 - 3
    - (t1 + t2 - 3) = (d - 70)/70 - 16/9
    - (t1 + t2) = (d - 70)/70 - 16/9 + 3
    - (t1 + t2) = (d - 70)/70 - 7/9
  - We can now substitute the expressions we derived for t1 and t2:
    - (d/70) + (d/90) = (d - 70)/70 - 7/9
    - Multiplying both sides by 630 (the LCM of 70 and 90) to eliminate the denominators:
    - 9d + 7d = 9(d - 70) - 70(7)
    - 16d = 9d - 630
    - 7d = -630
    - d = -90
  - Since distance cannot be negative, we can conclude that there must be an error in the problem statement or in our calculations. Therefore, the answer is None of the above.

  - The formula to find the average speed is: Average speed = Total distance / Total time
  - If Kevin drives at a constant speed of 70 mph from A to B, and then at a constant speed of 90 mph from B to A, then his average speed for the entire trip is: Average speed = (2 x distance AB) / (time AB + time BA)
  - We know that 3 hours before the end of his trip, Kevin was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it. This means that he had already driven for (time AB - 3) hours on his way back from B to A.
  
Solution:
  - Let's assume that the distance between A and B is x.
  - The time it takes Kevin to drive from A to B at 70 mph is: time AB = x / 70
  - The time it takes Kevin to drive from B to A at 90 mph is: time BA = x / 90
  - Kevin's average speed for the entire trip is: Average speed = (2x) / (time AB + time BA) = (2x) / (x/70 + x/90)
  - Simplifying the above equation, we get: Average speed = (2x) / (9x/630) = 140
  - We know that 3 hours before the end of his trip, Kevin was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it. This means that he had already driven for (time AB - 3) hours on his way back from B to A.
  - Using the formula Distance = Speed x Time, we can calculate the distance Kevin covered in (time AB - 3) hours at 90 mph: distance = 90 x (time AB - 3) = 90(x/90 - 3) = x - 270
  - This means that at that point, Kevin had already covered a distance of (x - 270) miles on his way back from B to A.
  - The total distance between A and B is the sum of the distance Kevin covered on his way from A to B, the distance he covered on his way back from B to A before the 3-hour mark, and the remaining 70 miles: x = x + (x - 270) + 70
  - Simplifying the above equation, we get: 3x = 640
  - Therefore, the distance between A and B is x = 213.33, which is closest to answer C: 270.
Action: Answer("C")

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 97 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: An organization decided to raise Rs. 6 lakh by collecting equal contribution from each of its employees. If each of them had contributed Rs. 60 extra, the contribution would have been Rs. 6.24 lakh. How many employees are there in that organization?
Choices:
  A: 300
  B: 200
  C: 400
  D: 100
  E: 500
Response 0:
Let's assume that there are x employees in the organization and each of them contributes y amount. 

From the problem, we know that:
xy = 6,00,000   ------ (1) 

If each person contributes an extra Rs. 60, then the new contribution per person will be y + 60.
Hence, the total new contribution will be:
(x)*(y+60) = 6,24,000

Expanding the above equation, we get:
xy + 60x = 6,24,000

Substituting the value of xy from equation (1), we get:
6,00,000 + 60x = 6,24,000

Solving for x, we get:
x = 400

Therefore, there are 400 employees in the organization.

Action: Answer("C")

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 5.0 | Problem 98 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A man divides Rs 8600 among 5 sons, 4 daughters and 2 nephews. If each daughter receives four times as much as each nephew, and each son receives five as much as each nephew. How much does each daughter receive ?
Choices:
  A: Rs 400
  B: Rs 500
  C: Rs 600
  D: Rs 700
  E: Rs 800
Response 0:
Let the share of each nephew be x. Then, the share of each daughter is 4x and the share of each son is 5x.

The total number of people who receive a share is 5+4+2=11.

The total amount to be divided is Rs 8600.

So, we can set up the following equation:
5(5x) + 4(4x) + 2(x) = 8600

Simplifying this equation, we get:
25x + 16x + 2x = 8600
43x = 8600
x = 200

So, each nephew receives Rs 200.

Each daughter receives 4 times as much as each nephew, which is 4x = 4(200) = Rs 800.

Therefore, the answer is (E) Rs 800. 

Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Let's assume that each nephew receives X amount of money. 
So, each daughter receives 4X amount of money.
And, each son receives 5X amount of money.

So, the total amount of money given to the nephews = 2X
The total amount of money given to the daughters = 4 × 2X = 8X
The total amount of money given to the sons = 5 × 2X = 10X

Total number of recipients = 5 sons + 4 daughters + 2 nephews = 11

Total amount of money given = Rs 8600

So, 11X = 8600

X = 780

Therefore, each daughter receives 4X = 4 × 780 = Rs 3120.

Choices:
  A: 1584
  B: 2520
  C: 1728
  D: 1656
  E: None

Knowledge:

  A fraction of a number can be found by multiplying the number with the fraction.
  The student found 7/18 of the number instead of 7/8 of the number.
  The difference between the actual value and the value found by the student is 770.
  We can form an equation using the above information: 7/8 * x - 7/18 * x = 770
  We can simplify the equation: 35x/72 - 14x/72 = 770
  We can solve for x: 21x/72 = 770
  x = 2640

Topic: Math
Question: Calculate the maximum distance you can travel with $8.50 on a cab which charges $3.50 for the first quarter-mile and 10 cents for each additional quarter mile.
Choices:
  A: 11.75 miles
  B: 12.75 miles
  C: 17.75 miles
  D: 14.75 miles
  E: 10.75 miles
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The cab charges $3.50 for the first quarter-mile and 10 cents for each additional quarter mile.
  We want to know the maximum distance that can be traveled with $8.50.
  
Solution:
  Let's assume that the maximum distance you can travel is x miles.
  The cost of traveling the first quarter-mile is $3.50.
  The cost of traveling the remaining distance (x - 0.25) miles is $0.10 for each quarter mile, or $0.40 for each mile.
  So the total cost of the trip is $3.50 + $0.40(x - 0.25).
  We want to find the maximum distance x that can be traveled with $8.50, so we set the total cost equal to $8.50 and solve for x:
  
  $3.50 + $0.40(x - 0.25) = $8.50
  
  $0.40(x - 0.25) = $5.00
  
  x - 0.25 = 12.5
  
  x = 12.75
  
  Therefore, the maximum distance that can be traveled with $8.50 is 12.75 miles.
  
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  The cab charges $3.50 for the first quarter-mile and 10 cents for each additional quarter mile. 
  To find the maximum distance that can be traveled with $8.50, we need to divide the remaining amount after the initial charge by the charge per quarter mile.
  $8.50 - $3.50 = $5.00
  $5.00 ÷ $0.10 = 50 quarters = 12.5 miles
